09/11/23, 10:08 am - Utkarsh: To determine whether a relation R is in Second Normal Form (2NF), we need to check two conditions:

1. R must be in 1NF (First Normal Form).
2. For each non-prime attribute A (an attribute not part of any candidate key), every partial dependency on a candidate key is eliminated.

Given relation R(A, B, C, D) and the functional dependency set FD={AB->CD, B->C}, let's analyze it:

1. **1NF Check:** First, ensure that R is in 1NF. A relation is in 1NF if it contains only atomic (indivisible) values. In this case, the relation R already satisfies this condition as it has individual attributes A, B, C, and D.

2. **Candidate Keys:** To identify candidate keys, we need to consider the given functional dependencies. The closure of an attribute set will help us find potential candidate keys. In this case, we have FD={AB->CD, B->C}.

   - Closure of AB:
     - AB+ = AB (by reflexivity)
     - AB+ = ABCD (using FD AB->CD)

   - Closure of B:
     - B+ = B (by reflexivity)
     - B+ = BC (using FD B->C)
     - B+ = ABCD (using FD AB->CD and B->C)

   From the closure calculations, we can see that both AB and B can be candidate keys since they can determine all attributes (AB+ and B+ both contain all attributes A, B, C, D).

3. **2NF Check:** Now, let's check for partial dependencies. For a relation to be in 2NF, non-prime attributes (attributes not part of any candidate key) must not be partially dependent on a candidate key.

   In this case, C and D are non-prime attributes. Since both AB and B are candidate keys, we need to check if C and D are partially dependent on either AB or B.

   - FD AB->CD implies that C and D are functionally dependent on AB, which is a candidate key. So, C and D are not partially dependent on AB.

   - FD B->C implies that C is functionally dependent on B, which is a candidate key. So, C is not partially dependent on B.

Since C and D are not partially dependent on either candidate key (AB or B), the relation R is in 2NF.

Therefore, no further conversion is needed to achieve 2NF for this relation. It already satisfies the 2NF requirements.

09/12/23, 10:14 am - Siddharth Singh: #include <iostream>
#include <sstream>
#include <cmath>

std::string num_to_words(int num) {
    std::string words[] = {"zero", "one", "two", "three", "four", "five", "six", "seven", "eight", "nine"};
    return words[num];
}

std::string get_scientific_notation(double num, const std::string& name) {
    std::ostringstream oss;
    oss << std::scientific << num;

    std::string num_str = oss.str();
    std::size_t e_pos = num_str.find('e');

    double coefficient = std::stod(num_str.substr(0, e_pos));
    int exponent = std::stoi(num_str.substr(e_pos + 1));

    int single_digit_coefficient = static_cast<int>(coefficient) % 9;
    single_digit_coefficient = (single_digit_coefficient == 0) ? 9 : single_digit_coefficient;

    int single_digit_exponent = std::abs(exponent) % 9;
    single_digit_exponent = (single_digit_exponent == 0) ? 9 : single_digit_exponent;

    std::string s1 = num_to_words(single_digit_coefficient).substr(0, 3) + "e" + num_to_words(single_digit_exponent).substr(0, 3);

    std::string s2;
    if (single_digit_exponent % 2 == 1) {
        for (std::size_t i = 0; i < name.length(); i += 2) {
            s2 += name[i];
        }
    } else {
        for (std::size_t i = 1; i < name.length(); i += 2) {
            s2 += name[i];
        }
    }

    return s1 + "@" + s2;
}

int main() {
    int t;
    std::cin >> t;

    for (int i = 0; i < t; ++i) {
        double number;
        std::string name;
        std::cin >> number >> name;

        // Check if the name is valid
        bool valid_name = true;
        for (char c : name) {
            if (!islower(c)) {
                valid_name = false;
                break;
            }
        }

        if (!valid_name) {
            std::cout << "Invalid input" << std::endl;
            continue;
        }

        std::string password = get_scientific_notation(number, name);
        std::cout << password << std::endl;
    }

    return 0;
}

09/12/23, 12:10 pm - Siddharth Singh: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <cmath>
#include <algorithm>
#include <map>

using namespace std;

struct Point {
    int x, y;
};

struct Entity {
    string name;
    Point location;
};

struct DistanceInfo {
    int distance;
    string vehicleNumber;
};

int calculateManhattanDistance(Point p1, Point p2) {
    return abs(p1.x - p2.x) + abs(p1.y - p2.y);
}

bool compareLexicographically(const string& s1, const string& s2) {
    return s1 < s2;
}

int main() {
    int N, M;
    cin >> N >> M;

    vector<Entity> passengers(N);
    vector<Entity> vehicles(M);

    for (int i = 0; i < N; ++i) {
        cin >> passengers[i].name >> passengers[i].location.x >> passengers[i].location.y;
    }

    for (int i = 0; i < M; ++i) {
        cin >> vehicles[i].name >> vehicles[i].location.x >> vehicles[i].location.y;
    }

    map<string, bool> vehicleAssigned;

    int totalDistance = 0;

    for (const auto& passenger : passengers) {
        vector<DistanceInfo> distances;

        for (const auto& vehicle : vehicles) {
            if (!vehicleAssigned[vehicle.name]) {
                int distance = calculateManhattanDistance(passenger.location, vehicle.location);
                distances.push_back({distance, vehicle.name});
            }
        }

        sort(distances.begin(), distances.end(), [](const DistanceInfo& d1, const DistanceInfo& d2) {
            if (d1.distance != d2.distance) {
                return d1.distance < d2.distance;
            } else {
                return compareLexicographically(d1.vehicleNumber, d2.vehicleNumber);
            }
        });

        totalDistance += distances[0].distance;
        vehicleAssigned[distances[0].vehicleNumber] = true;
    }
    cout<<totalDistance;

    return 0;
}
09/12/23, 12:37 pm - Vaibhav CS-AI: weights = list(map(int, input().split()))
weights.sort(reverse=True)

load = int(input())

vehicles = 0
i, j = 0, len(weights) - 1

while i <= j:
    if weights[i] + weights[j] <= load:
        i += 1
        j -= 1
    else:
        i += 1
    vehicles += 1

print(vehicles, end="")
09/12/23, 1:04 pm - Siddharth Singh: Warehouse Code
Python 
TCS Codevita
Technical Study Ajay

def minimum_vehicles(weights, max_limit):
    sorted_weights = sorted(filter(lambda x: x != 0, weights), reverse=True)

    left, right = 0, len(sorted_weights) - 1
    vehicles = 0

    while left <= right:
        if sorted_weights[left] + sorted_weights[right] <= max_limit:
            right -= 1
        left += 1
        vehicles += 1

    return vehicles

weights = list(map(int, input().split()))
max_limit = int(input())

result = minimum_vehicles(weights, max_limit)
print(result, end="")

    sorted_custom_weights = sorted(filter(lambda x: x != 0, custom_weights), reverse=True)

    left_ptr, right_ptr = 0, len(sorted_custom_weights) - 1
    num_vehicles = 0

    while left_ptr <= right_ptr:
        if sorted_custom_weights[left_ptr] + sorted_custom_weights[right_ptr] <= custom_max_limit:
            right_ptr -= 1
        left_ptr += 1
        num_vehicles += 1

    return num_vehicles

custom_weights = list(map(int, input().split()))
custom_max_limit = int(input())

result = minimum_vehicles(custom_weights, custom_max_limit)
print(result, end="")

import math

def calculate_distance(point1, point2):
    return abs(point1[0] - point2[0]) + abs(point1[1] - point2[1])

def assign_vehicles(passengers, vehicles):
    allocated_vehicles = {}
    total_distance = 0

    for passenger in sorted(passengers):
        placementlelo = math.inf
        closest_vehicle = ""
        passenger_coordinates = passengers[passenger]

        for vehicle in vehicles:
            if vehicles[vehicle] == "":
                vehicle_coordinates = vehicles[vehicle + "_coordinates"]
                distance = calculate_distance(passenger_coordinates, vehicle_coordinates)
                if distance < placementlelo or (distance == placementlelo and vehicle < closest_vehicle):
                    placementlelo = distance
                    closest_vehicle = vehicle
        
        allocated_vehicles[passenger] = closest_vehicle
        vehicles[closest_vehicle] = passenger
        total_distance += placementlelo

    return total_distance
N, M = map(int, input().split())
passengers = {}
vehicles = {}

for _ in range(N):
    name, x, y = input().split()
    passengers[name] = (int(x), int(y))

for _ in range(M):
    vehicle, x, y = input().split()
    vehicles[vehicle] = ""
    vehicles[vehicle + "_coordinates"] = (int(x), int(y))
minimum_distance = assign_vehicles(passengers, vehicles)
print(minimum_distance,end="")

09/12/23, 2:00 pm - Vaibhav CS-AI: from collections import defaultdict 

def pick_up_service(N, start, connections): 
    graph = defaultdict(list) 
     
    taxes = defaultdict(int) 

    for i in range(N - 1): 
        city1, city2, goods, tax = connections[i] 
        # graph[city1].update({city2: (goods, tax)}) 
        # graph[city2].update({city1: (goods, tax)}) 
        graph[city1].append((-1 * goods, tax, city2)) 
        taxes[city2] = tax 


    route = [] 

    # print(graph) 
    def dfs(city): 
        route.append(city) 
        for n in sorted(graph[city]): 
            dfs(n[2]) 
            route.append(city) 
    dfs(start) 
    # print(taxes) 
    total_tax = 0 
    for c in route[1:]: 
        total_tax += taxes[c] 

    return route, total_tax 



N = int(input()) 

# print("n is ", N) 
# print("r is ", r.split('\n')) 

cons = [] 

for _ in range(N-1): 
    l = input() 
    ls = l.split() 
    cons.append((ls[0], ls[1], int(ls[2]), int(ls[3]))) 
   


ans, t = pick_up_service(N, cons[0][0], cons) 

print("-".join(ans)) 
print(t, end="")

Whittle Code ✅✅✅ 
 
def calculate_area(nails): 
    x_coords = [nail[0] for nail in nails] 
    y_coords = [nail[1] for nail in nails] 
 
    min_x = min(x_coords) 
    max_x = max(x_coords) 
    min_y = min(y_coords) 
    max_y = max(y_coords) 
 
    return (max_x - min_x) * (max_y - min_y) 
 
def pick_nails(nails, m): 
    result = [] 
    while m > 0: 
        min_area = float('inf') 
        nail_to_remove = None 
 
        for i, nail in enumerate(nails): 
            remaining_nails = nails[:i] + nails[i + 1:] 
            current_area = calculate_area(remaining_nails) 
 
            if current_area < min_area: 
                min_area = current_area 
                nail_to_remove = nail 
 
        result.append(nail_to_remove) 
        nails.remove(nail_to_remove) 
        m -= 1 
 
    return result 
 
def can_win_game(nails, m): 
    initial_area = calculate_area(nails) 
    picked_nails = pick_nails(nails.copy(), m) 
    final_area = calculate_area(picked_nails) 
 
    return final_area == 0, picked_nails 
 
# Input the number of nails 
N = int(input()) 
 
# Input coordinates of nails 
nails = [list(map(int, input().split())) for _ in range(N)] 
 
# Input the maximum number of nails a player can pick in their turn 
m = int(input()) 
 
# Determine if the game can be won and print the result 
can_win, picked_nails = can_win_game(nails, m) 
 
for nail in picked_nails: 
    print(*nail) 
 
print("YES" if can_win else "NO")
